style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(iii)       enter into and inspect any market, godown, shop, stall or other place used for the manufacture, storage or sale of any apparatus, utensil or vessel ordinarily used or intended to be used or likely to be used for preparing, manufacturing or containing any food.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If any such food as is mentioned in sub-section (1) or clause (i) of sub-section (2) appears to the Inspector to be injurious to health, unwholesome, unfit for human consumption, or not of the nature, substance or quality which it purports to be, or as not fulfilling the prescribed conditions subject to which such food is to be prepared, manufactured, kept, stored or sold or if any such apparatus or utensil as is mentioned in clause (ii) of sub-section (2) is of such kind or in such state as to render any food prepared, manufactured or contained therein unwholesome or unfit for human consumption or injurious to health, he may seize and remove such food, apparatus or utensil to be dealt with as hereinafter provided.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) An Inspector may, instead of removing any food, apparatus or utensil seized under sub-section (3), leave the same in the custody of the person from whose possession, custody or control the same was seized or in such safe custody as he may deem fit, so as to be dealt with as hereinafter provided and may, at any time hereafter, remove the same to the custody of the local authority concerned.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) When any food, apparatus or utensil is seized under sub-section (3), it may be destroyed by the Inspector with the consent in writing of the owners or the person from whose possession, custody or control it is seized.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(6) If any food seized under sub-section (3) is of a perishable nature and is, in the opinion of the Inspector, unsound, unwholesome or unfit for human consumption, it may be destroyed without such consent but in the presence of two respectable witnesses.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(7) An Inspector shall prepare a statement of the food, apparatus or utensil seized and shall deliver a copy thereof to the local authority and to the person from whose custody the food, apparatus or utensil is seized or, if such person be not present, send such copy to him by post.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(8) Any person claiming anything seized under sub-section (3) may, within seven days of the seizure, complain to any Magistrate of the first class having jurisdiction at the place of seizure, and the Magistrate may, after making such enquiry as he may deem necessary, confirm or disallow such seizure, wholly or in part, and order such article, or the part or parts thereof of which seizure has been disallowed, to be restored to the claimant.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(9) If the Magistrate confirms the seizure, he may direct that the food, apparatus or utensil seized shall be-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) forfeited to the local authority; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii)        destroyed or disposed of at the cost of the owner or person from whose possession, custody or control it was seized, in such manner as to prevent the same from being sold, or kept, or stored, or used as food or for the preparation or manufacture of, or for containing, any food.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(10) If no complaint is made within the period specified in sub-section (8), the article of food or the apparatus or utensil seized shall be forfeited to the local authority.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">PART IV</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">FOOD ANALYSIS</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Public Analyst</p><p style="text-align: justify;">17. The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, appoint a person to be a Public Analyst for the purposes of this Act for any area in respect of all or any specified food.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Purchase of samples, etc</p><p style="text-align: justify;">18. (1) An Inspector may, for the purpose of analysis, purchase a sample of food-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) in transit,</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        sold, offered for sale, hawked about, kept or stored or received for the purpose of preparing therewith any food, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        kept or stored in a market, godown, shop, stall, hotel, restaurant or eating-house for the purpose of trade or sale or received therein for the purpose of preparing or manufacturing therewith any food.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) No person shall refuse to sell any food to an Inspector intending to purchase such food for the purpose of sub-section (1) in such reasonable quantity and from such container as he may ask for.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- The purchase or sale of a sample of any food for the purpose of analysis under this Act shall be deemed to be purchased or sold for human consumption or use.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If, in contravention of sub-section (2), any person refuses to sell, the Inspector may, without prejudice to any penalty to which such person may be liable for such contravention, seize such quantity of the food as may appear to him to be necessary, and shall give such person a certificate showing the price, nature and quantity of the food seized, the date, time and place of seizure, and, on demand being made in that behalf, the price of the food seized.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) The Inspector shall prepare, in such form as may be prescribed, a declaration in triplicate, containing full particulars, relating to the sample seized and such declaration shall be signed or marked both by the Inspector and the person from whose possession, custody or control the food has been seized and a copy thereof shall be given to such person.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) When a sample is taken from the stock in the possession of a commission agent, he shall be bound to give the name and such other particulars of the person on whose behalf such stock is held by him as the Inspector may require.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Right of private persons to have samples analysed</p><p style="text-align: justify;">19. (1) Any person may make an application in writing to an Inspector asking him to purchase a sample of such food and from such person as may be specified in the application and to submit such sample to the Public Analyst for analysis.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The cost of the sample purchased and of the analysis done under sub-section (1) shall be payable by the person making the application:</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that, in case the sample is found by the Public Analyst to be adulterated, any amount paid by the applicant under this sub-section shall be refunded to him.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Action in respect of samples</p><p style="text-align: justify;">20. (1) An Inspector shall, as soon as he has purchased or seized any food with the intention of submitting the same for analysis, divide the food into three parts and mark, seal or fasten each such part in such manner as the nature of the food may require, and also permit the person from whom the sample is taken, if such person so desires, to affix his own seal or mark on each of the three parts.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Inspector shall-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        deliver one part of the food divided under sub-section (1) to the person from whom the food is purchased or seized;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) retain with him one part for future comparison; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) submit one part to the Public Analyst, to be examined by him on payment of such fee as may be prescribed:</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that, where the sample is taken from any food which is about to be imported or in transit or at the place of delivery to the purchaser, consumer or consignee, or is unclaimed, the part of the sample to be delivered under clause (a) shall be retained by the Inspector, unless the name and address of the consignor appear on the container from which the sample is taken, in which case he shall forward that part of the sample to the consignor by registered post or otherwise, together with a notice informing him that the sample would be analysed by the Public Analyst.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Certificate of Public Analyst</p><p style="text-align: justify;">21. (1) The Public Analyst upon receiving sample of food from an Inspector shall, as soon as possible, analyse the same and issue to the Inspector a certificate in the prescribed form showing the result of the analysis.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The person from whom the article so analysed was purchased or seized may, on payment of the prescribed fee, obtain from the Public Analyst a copy of the certificate issued under sub-section (1).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) No person shall display or otherwise use any copy of the certificate for purposes of advertisement.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power of Government to seize sample</p><p style="text-align: justify;">22. (1) The Government may, in relation to any matter appearing to it to affect the general interest of the consumers of any food, direct any public servant to procure for analysis a sample of such food, and thereupon such public servant shall have all the powers of an Inspector.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The public servant upon receiving the certificate of the Public Analyst shall take proceedings or cause proceedings to be taken as if he himself had caused such analysis to be made.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The expenses incurred by the public servant in performing such duties shall be paid by the local authority.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">PART V</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">PENALTIES AND PROCEDURE</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Penalties</p><p style="text-align: justify;">23. (1) Whoever contravenes any of the provisions of section 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11 or 13 shall be punished-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        for a first offence, with rigorous imprisonment for a term which may extend to six months and with fine which shall not be less than one hundred Taka or more than two thousand Taka and also with whipping;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        for a second offence, with rigorous imprisonment for a term not less than three months and not more than two years and with fine which shall not be less than five hundred Taka or more than ten thousand Taka and also with whipping; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        for repeated offences or for offences of large scale adulteration or adulteration with injurious substances even in the first instance, with rigorous imprisonment for a term which shall not be less than three years or more than five years and with fine which shall not be less than five thousand Taka or more than one lakh Taka and also with whipping.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Whoever contravenes any of the provisions of section 12, 18, 21 or 28 or of any rules shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to one year and with fine.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Any person who attempts to contravene, or abets the contravention of any of the provisions mentioned in sub-section (1) or sub-section (2) shall be punishable with the same punishment as is provided for such contravention.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) All fines recovered under this Act shall be credited to the fund of the local authority within the limits of whose jurisdiction the offence for which the fine was imposed was committed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) Where in the course of any business a person commits an offence under this Act and is convicted therefore under clause (b) or clause (c) of sub-section (1) and such business is carried on by him or by any other person on his behalf he or such other person shall, for a period of one year from the date of such conviction, prominently display on the premises in which such business is carried on a notice of the fact of such conviction, and, on his failing to so display such notice, shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three months or with fine or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to try summarily</p><p style="text-align: justify;">24. Any Magistrate for the time being empowered to try in a summary way the offences specified in sub-section (1) of section 260 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, may try summarily any offence made punishable under sub-section (1) and sub-section (2) of section 23 of this Act in accordance with the provisions of Chapter XXII of that Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Certain things to be presumed</p><p style="text-align: justify;">25. In every prosecution under this Act, the Court shall presume-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) that any food found in the possession of any person who is or has been habitually found preparing, manufacturing, keeping, storing, selling or offering or exposing for sale or hawking about such food was being prepared, manufactured, kept, stored, sold, offered or exposed for sale or hawked about by such person;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) that any food commonly used for human consumption, kept, stored, sold or offered for sale, was kept, stored, sold or offered for sale for human consumption;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) that any food commonly used for human consumption which is found on any premises used for the preparation or manufacture of such food was prepared or manufactured for human consumption;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) that any substance capable of being used in the preparation or manufacture of any food commonly used for human consumption which is found on any premises in which such food is prepared or manufactured was intended to be used in the preparation or manufacture of such food; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) that any food is not of the nature, substance or quality it purports to be if it is deficient in any of its normal constituents to the extent specified in the rules or if any extraneous matter has been added to it in contravention of the rules.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Declaration under section 18 to be evidence</p><p style="text-align: justify;">26. A declaration signed or marked under sub-section (4) of section 18 may be produced as evidence of the facts contained therein in any inquiry, trial or other proceedings under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Certificate of Public Analyst to be evidence of fact stated therein</p><p style="text-align: justify;">27. (1) The production in any inquiry, trial or other proceedings under this Act of a certificate under the hand of a Public Analyst in the form prescribed shall, until the contrary is proved, be sufficient to prove the facts therein stated.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) When any person is accused of an offence under this Act, he may request the Court to summon as a witness the Public Analyst who analysed the sample in respect of which he is accused of having committed an offence and the Court may, and, in every case in which the accused deposits in the Court a sum of money in accordance with the scale prescribed, shall, summon the Public Analyst, and if such person is acquitted, any sum of money so deposited shall be refunded to him.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Analysis by Chemical Examiner</p><p style="text-align: justify;">28. (1) The Court may of its own accord or on the request of the accused cause any food or sample of food to be sent for analysis to the Chemical Examiner who shall thereupon analyse the same and report the results of the analysis to the Court in the form prescribed and the cost of such analysis shall be paid by the accused if the Court so directs.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The certificate of the Chemical Examiner shall, until the contrary is proved, be sufficient to prove the facts therein stated.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) No person shall display or otherwise use the report of the Chemical Examiner for purposes of advertisement.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">What shall or shall not be a good defence</p><p style="text-align: justify;">29. (1) In any prosecution under this Act, it shall be no defence to allege-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        that the accused was ignorant of the nature, substance or quality of the food; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        that the purchaser having purchased only for purposes of analysis was not prejudiced.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The seller shall not be deemed to have committed an offence under this Act if he proves-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        that the food sold was purchased or obtained as agent by him with written warranty to the effect that it was of the same nature, substance or quality as that demanded by the purchaser;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        that at the time he sold it he had no reason to believe that the food was not of such nature, substance or quality as that demanded by the purchaser; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) that he sold it in the same state in which he had purchased it.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) No evidence of a warranty under clause (a) of sub-section (2) shall be admissible on behalf of the seller unless-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        the seller has, within seven days of the service of the summons upon him, sent to the Inspector a copy of the warranty with a notice stating that he intends to rely on it and specifying the name and address of the person from whom he received it and has also sent a like notice of his intention to that person; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        such warranty is given by person permanently residing or carrying on business in 5[ Bangladesh].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) The Court shall summon the warrantor as a co-accused if it admits the warranty on behalf of the seller.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Forfeiture of food upon conviction</p><p style="text-align: justify;">30. In the case of any conviction under this Act, the Court may order that any food to which the conviction relates, together with all packages or utensils containing the same, shall be forfeited to the Government or shall be disposed of in such manner as may be specified in the order.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Expenses of analysis</p><p style="text-align: justify;">31. When any person is convicted of an offence under this Act, the Court shall order that all fees and other expenses incidental to the analysis of any food in respect of which the conviction is made, which shall, in no case be less than thirty Taka, be paid by the person convicted, in addition to the fine which he may be sentenced to pay, and the amount of such fees and expenses shall be recovered as if it were a fine.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Trial of offence</p><p style="text-align: justify;">32. (1) No Court shall take cognizance of any offence punishable under this Act except on a report in writing of the facts constituting such offence made by an Inspector authorised in this behalf by the Director or the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) No Court inferior to that of a Magistrate of the first class shall try an offence under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">PART VI</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">MISCELLANEOUS</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Indemnity</p><p style="text-align: justify;">33. No suit, prosecution or other legal proceedings shall lie against any person for anything which is in good faith done or intended to be done in pursuance of any provision of this Act or any rule, order or direction made or given thereunder.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Inspector, etc, to be public servant</p><p style="text-align: justify;">34. An Inspector while performing any of his functions under this Act and all other persons assisting him in the performance of such functions shall be deemed to be public servants within the meaning of section 21 of the 6[ * * *] Penal Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to make rules</p><p style="text-align: justify;">35. (1) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make rules for carrying out the purpose of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In particular and without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power, such rules may provide for all or any of the following matters, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the standards, specifications, normal constituents and quality of food;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        the qualifications of persons who may be appointed Public Analysts for the purpose of this Act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) the regulation of appointment and qualifications of persons to be appointed as Inspectors;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) the methods of analysis to be followed by Public Analysts for the analysis of any food and the form of the certificate;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) the fees to be paid in respect of the analysis of any food by a Public Analyst;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) the prohibition of use of any particular matter or ingredient in the preparation or manufacture of any food;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) the conditions (including the addition of a colour or any other substance) subject to which any food shall be prepared, manufactured, kept, stored, sold or offered or exposed for sale;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h) the prohibition of keeping or storage for sale of foods other than those approved under the rules;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) the cleanliness and freedom from contamination of any food in the course of its preparation, manufacture, storage, packing, carriage, delivery or exposure for sale, and the cleanliness or places, receptacles, packages, wrappings, appliances and vehicles used in such preparation, manufacture, storage, packing, carriage or delivery;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="&lt;/div"></p></div><div class="popular-posts widget widget_categories"><h3 class="widget-title"><span>Disclaimer:</span></h3><div class="widget-content" style="text-align:justify;"><p>The 339	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">         THE CARRIAGE BY AIR (INTERNATIONAL CONVENTION) ACT, 1966 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE CARRIAGE BY AIR (INTERNATIONAL CONVENTION) ACT, 1966 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ACT NO. IX OF 1966).[18th June, 1966]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to give effect in Bangladesh to the Convention concerning international carriage by air known as “the Warsaw Convention as amended at The Hague, 1955”.   1</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to give effect in Bangladesh to the Convention concerning international carriage by air known as “the Warsaw Convention as amended at The Hague, 1955”, and to enable the rules contained in that Convention to be applied, subject to exceptions, adaptations and modifications, to carriage by air in Bangladesh which is not international carriage within the meaning of the Convention, and to provide for matters connected herewith;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Carriage by Air (International Convention) Act, 1966.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once and shall be deemed to have taken effect on the first day of August, 1963.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Application of the Warsaw Convention, as amended, to Bangladesh</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. (1) The rules contained in the First Schedule, being the provisions of the Convention for the unification of certain rules relating to international carriage by air known as “the Warsaw Convention as amended at The Hague, 1955”, hereinafter referred to as the Convention, shall, subject to the provisions of this Act, have the force of law in Bangladesh in relation to any carriage by air to which those rules apply, irrespective of the nationality of the aircraft performing the carriage.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, certify who are the High Contracting Parties to the Convention, in respect of what territories they are parties, and to what extent they have availed themselves of the Additional Protocol to the Convention, and any such notification shall be conclusive evidence of the matters certified therein.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Notwithstanding anything contained in the Fatal Accidents Act, 1855, or any other law for the time being in force, the rules contained in the First Schedule shall, in all cases to which those rules apply, determine the liability of a carrier in respect of the death of a passenger, and the rules contained in the Second Schedule shall determine the persons by whom and for whose benefit and the manner in which such liability may be enforced.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) Any sum in francs mentioned in rule 22 of the First Schedule shall, for the purpose of any action against a carrier, be converted into rupees at the rate of exchange prevailing on the date on which the amount of damages to be paid by the carrier is ascertained by the Court.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) Any reference in the First Schedule-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        to the territory of any High Contracting Party to the Convention shall be construed as a reference to all the territories in respect of which he is a party; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        to agents of the carrier shall be construed as including a reference to servants of the carrier.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provisions regarding suits against High Contracting Parties who undertake carriage by air</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. (1) Every High Contracting Party to the Convention who has not availed himself of the provisions of the Additional Protocol thereto shall, for the purposes of any suit brought in a Court in Bangladesh in accordance with the provisions of rule 28 of the First Schedule to enforce a claim in respect of carriage undertaken by him, be deemed to have submitted to the jurisdiction of that Court and to be a person for the purposes of the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The 2[ High Court Division] may make rules of procedure providing for all matters which may be expedient to enable such suits to be instituted and carried on.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Nothing in this section shall authorise any Court to attach or sell any property of a High Contracting Party to the Convention.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Application of Act to carriage by air which is not international</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, apply the rules contained in the First Schedule and any provision of section 2 to such carriage by air, not being international carriage by air as defined in the First Schedule, as may be specified in the notification, subject, however, to such exceptions, adaptations and modifications, if any, as may be so specified.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Repeal, etc</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. The Carriage By Air Act, 1934, shall,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        in so far as it relates to carriage by air to which the rules contained in the First Schedule to this Act may, for the time being, apply, stand repealed; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) to the extent it has not been so repealed, have effect subject to the modification that for the provisions of the Second Schedule to that Act the provisions of the Second Schedule to this Act shall be substituted.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the words “Bangladesh” and “Government” were substituted for the words “Pakistan” and “Central Government” respectively by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “High Court Division” were substituted for the words “High Court” by Article 7(1)(a) of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972) as amended by the Bangladesh Adaptation of Existing Laws (Amendment) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 150 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
340	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE CARRIAGE BY AIR (SUPPLEMENTARY CONVENTION) ACT, 1968 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE CARRIAGE BY AIR (SUPPLEMENTARY CONVENTION) ACT, 1968 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ACT NO. V OF 1968).[29th  May, 1968]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to give effect in Bangladesh to the Convention, Supplementary to the Warsaw Convention, for the Unification of Certain Rules Relating to International Carriage by Air Performed by a Person other than the Contracting Carrier.           1</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to give effect in Bangladesh to the Convention, Supplementary to the Warsaw Convention, for the Unification of Certain Rules Relating to International Carriage by Air Performed by a Person other than the Contracting Carrier, and to provide for matters connected therewith;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Carriage by Air (Supplementary Convention) Act, 1968.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once and shall be deemed to have taken effect on the 19th day of September, 1965.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Application of Supplementary Convention</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. (1) The rules contained in the Schedule, being the provisions of the Convention, Supplementary to the Warsaw Convention, for the Unification of Certain Rules Relating to International Carriage by Air Performed by a Person other than the Contracting Carrier, hereinafter referred to as the Convention, shall, subject to the provisions of this Act, have the force of law in Bangladesh in relation to any carriage by air to which those rules apply, irrespective of the nationality of the aircraft performing the carriage.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The rules contained in the Schedule shall be supplementary to, and form part of the rules contained in the First Schedule to the Carriage By Air Act, 1934 (XX of 1934), or, as the case may be, in the First Schedule to the Carriage by Air (International Convention) Act, 1966 (IX of 1966), and shall have effect accordingly.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The 2[ Government] may, by notification in the official Gazette, certify who are the Contracting States for the purposes of the Convention and in respect of what territories they are Contracting States; and any such notification shall be conclusive evidence of the matters specified therein.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the word “Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The word “Government” was substituted for the words “Central Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
341	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">      THE CONSERVATOR OF PORTS, LANDS AND BUILDINGS (RECOVERY OF POSSESSION) ACT, 1967 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE CONSERVATOR OF PORTS, LANDS AND BUILDINGS (RECOVERY OF POSSESSION) ACT, 1967 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ACT NO. III OF 1968).[4th March, 1968]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to provide for the speedy recovery of possession of lands and buildings belonging to the Conservator of Ports by evicting the outgoing lessees, licensees, and unauthorised occupants therefrom.    1</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to provide for speedy recovery of possession of lands or buildings belonging to the Conservator of Ports to which the provisions of the Ports Act, 1908 (Act XV of 1908) have been extended or may hereinafter be extended and for matters ancillary thereto;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Short title, application and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Conservator of Ports, Lands and Buildings (Recovery of Possession) Act, 1967.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It applies to all Ports to which the Provision of the Ports Act, 1908 (Act XV of 1908) have been extended or may hereinafter be extended by notification in the official Gazette.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “Allotment” means permission or license to occupy temporarily any premises or part thereof on an agreed rental or fee, without conferring any right or interest in respect thereof on the person to whom such permission or license has been granted;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “Conservator” means some officer or body of persons appointed as such under section 7 of the Ports Act, 1908 (Act XV of 1908);</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        “Lands or Buildings” means lands or building or part thereof which vests in, or is in possession or under the management or control of a conservator, and used or held for the purposes connected with the administration and working of a Port but does not include any land or building in respect of which any person has a right of property as mentioned in the Ports Act, 1908;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- Building includes the lands appurtenant thereto;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) “Lease” has the same meaning as assigned to it under section 105 of the Transfer of Property Act, 1882 (Act IV of 1882) and includes an allotment, and “lessee”, which includes his heirs, assigns, legal representative and all persons inducted by him into the demised land or building, shall be construed accordingly;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) “License” shall have the same meaning as assigned to it under section 52 of the Easements Act, 1882 (Act V of 1882);</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f ) “Port” means a Port to which the provisions of the Ports Act, 1908 (Act XV of 1908) have for the time being been extended or may be extended hereafter;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g)        “Prescribed” means prescribed by rules made under this Act by the Government;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h)        “Unauthorised occupant” means a person who is in occupation of any land or building without permission of or license from the Conservator, and includes-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         a person inducted into any land or building by original lessee or licensee of the land and buildings; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii)        a person who remains in occupation of land or building after determination of the lease or license in respect of such land and buildings.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Eviction of outgoing lessee, licensee and unauthorised occupants from the lands or buildings</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. (1) If, on the expiry, whether before or after commencement of this Act, of the period of any lease or license in respect of any land or building of which the Conservator is the lessor or licensor or on the determination of such lease or license on the ground of breach of covenant or in pursuance of the condition in the lease imposing any obligation on the lessee or the licensee to give up possession of the demised land or building in the event of such land or building being required for the purposes of the Conservator, the lessee or licensee refused or failed, or refuses or fails, to vacate and deliver vacant possession of such land or building to the Conservator, then, notwithstanding anything contained in any other law, for the time being in force, or any contract, the Conservator may, after giving him an opportunity of being heard, by notice, in writing, require such lessee or licensee to vacate and deliver vacant possession of such land or building to him and to remove structures, if any, erected or built thereon by him within such time as may be specified in the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If the Conservator is satisfied, after making such inquiry as he may think fit, that a person is an unauthorised occupant of any land or building, he may, after giving him an opportunity of being heard, by notice, in writing, require such person to vacate such land or building, and deliver vacant possession thereof to him and to remove structures, if any, erected or built thereon by him, within such time as may be specified in the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If any person, to whom a notice to vacate or to deliver vacant possession or to remove structures is served under sub-section (1) or sub-section (2) fails to comply with the notice, the Conservator shall take possession of such land or building and demolish such structures after the expiry of 30 days of the date of the service of the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) No person shall be evicted under sub-section (2) in between the sunset and the sunrise.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Appeal</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. (1) Any person aggrieved by an order under sub-section (1) or by a direction under sub-section (2) of section 3 may, within thirty days from the services of such order or direction, prefer an appeal to the Commissioner concerned who may, pending the disposal of the appeal, make such interlocutory order as he may think fit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The decision of the Commissioner in an appeal under sub-section (1) shall be final.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. A notice or order under section 3 shall be served in the manner as prescribed in the Civil Procedure Code (Act V of 1908).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. (1) The cost of demolition of structures under section 3, hereinafter in this section referred as the cost, shall be payable to the Conservator by the lessee, licensee or the unauthorised occupant evicted, as the case may be.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If the cost is not paid on demand, the Chairman, Inland Water Transport Authority may, on application by the Conservator and after giving the lessee, licensee or unauthorised occupant, as the case may be, an opportunity of being heard, cause the materials of structures demolished to be sold in auction in such manner as may be prescribed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If the sale proceeds exceed the cost, the excess amount shall be paid to the lessee or the unauthorised occupant.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Recovery of arrears of rent or fee</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. If any rent or fee payable in respect of any land or building has been in arrear on the date of the recovery of possession of such land or building, the amount due on account of such arrears, with interest, if any, accrued thereupon shall be recoverable as public demand under the Public Demands Recovery Act, 1913 (Act III of 1913).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Jurisdiction of Courts barred</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. No Court shall question anything done or purported to have been done by the Conservator under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Indemnity</p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. No suit or other legal proceeding shall lie against the Conservator or any other person in respect of anything which is, in good faith, done or intended to be done under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Delegation of powers</p><p style="text-align: justify;">10. The Conservator, may with, previous approval of the Government, delegate any or all of his powers and functions under this Act to such person as he may think fit and proper.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to make rules</p><p style="text-align: justify;">11. The Government may make rules for carrying out the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
342	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">  THE CONSERVATOR OF PORTS, LANDS AND BUILDINGS (RECOVERY OF POSSESSION) ACT, 1967 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE CONSERVATOR OF PORTS, LANDS AND BUILDINGS (RECOVERY OF POSSESSION) ACT, 1967 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ACT NO. III OF 1968).[4th March, 1968]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to provide for the speedy recovery of possession of lands and buildings belonging to the Conservator of Ports by evicting the outgoing lessees, licensees, and unauthorised occupants therefrom.    1</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to provide for speedy recovery of possession of lands or buildings belonging to the Conservator of Ports to which the provisions of the Ports Act, 1908 (Act XV of 1908) have been extended or may hereinafter be extended and for matters ancillary thereto;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Short title, application and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Conservator of Ports, Lands and Buildings (Recovery of Possession) Act, 1967.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It applies to all Ports to which the Provision of the Ports Act, 1908 (Act XV of 1908) have been extended or may hereinafter be extended by notification in the official Gazette.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “Allotment” means permission or license to occupy temporarily any premises or part thereof on an agreed rental or fee, without conferring any right or interest in respect thereof on the person to whom such permission or license has been granted;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “Conservator” means some officer or body of persons appointed as such under section 7 of the Ports Act, 1908 (Act XV of 1908);</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        “Lands or Buildings” means lands or building or part thereof which vests in, or is in possession or under the management or control of a conservator, and used or held for the purposes connected with the administration and working of a Port but does not include any land or building in respect of which any person has a right of property as mentioned in the Ports Act, 1908;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- Building includes the lands appurtenant thereto;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) “Lease” has the same meaning as assigned to it under section 105 of the Transfer of Property Act, 1882 (Act IV of 1882) and includes an allotment, and “lessee”, which includes his heirs, assigns, legal representative and all persons inducted by him into the demised land or building, shall be construed accordingly;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) “License” shall have the same meaning as assigned to it under section 52 of the Easements Act, 1882 (Act V of 1882);</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f ) “Port” means a Port to which the provisions of the Ports Act, 1908 (Act XV of 1908) have for the time being been extended or may be extended hereafter;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g)        “Prescribed” means prescribed by rules made under this Act by the Government;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h)        “Unauthorised occupant” means a person who is in occupation of any land or building without permission of or license from the Conservator, and includes-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         a person inducted into any land or building by original lessee or licensee of the land and buildings; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii)        a person who remains in occupation of land or building after determination of the lease or license in respect of such land and buildings.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Eviction of outgoing lessee, licensee and unauthorised occupants from the lands or buildings</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. (1) If, on the expiry, whether before or after commencement of this Act, of the period of any lease or license in respect of any land or building of which the Conservator is the lessor or licensor or on the determination of such lease or license on the ground of breach of covenant or in pursuance of the condition in the lease imposing any obligation on the lessee or the licensee to give up possession of the demised land or building in the event of such land or building being required for the purposes of the Conservator, the lessee or licensee refused or failed, or refuses or fails, to vacate and deliver vacant possession of such land or building to the Conservator, then, notwithstanding anything contained in any other law, for the time being in force, or any contract, the Conservator may, after giving him an opportunity of being heard, by notice, in writing, require such lessee or licensee to vacate and deliver vacant possession of such land or building to him and to remove structures, if any, erected or built thereon by him within such time as may be specified in the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If the Conservator is satisfied, after making such inquiry as he may think fit, that a person is an unauthorised occupant of any land or building, he may, after giving him an opportunity of being heard, by notice, in writing, require such person to vacate such land or building, and deliver vacant possession thereof to him and to remove structures, if any, erected or built thereon by him, within such time as may be specified in the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If any person, to whom a notice to vacate or to deliver vacant possession or to remove structures is served under sub-section (1) or sub-section (2) fails to comply with the notice, the Conservator shall take possession of such land or building and demolish such structures after the expiry of 30 days of the date of the service of the notice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) No person shall be evicted under sub-section (2) in between the sunset and the sunrise.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Appeal</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. (1) Any person aggrieved by an order under sub-section (1) or by a direction under sub-section (2) of section 3 may, within thirty days from the services of such order or direction, prefer an appeal to the Commissioner concerned who may, pending the disposal of the appeal, make such interlocutory order as he may think fit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The decision of the Commissioner in an appeal under sub-section (1) shall be final.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. A notice or order under section 3 shall be served in the manner as prescribed in the Civil Procedure Code (Act V of 1908).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. (1) The cost of demolition of structures under section 3, hereinafter in this section referred as the cost, shall be payable to the Conservator by the lessee, licensee or the unauthorised occupant evicted, as the case may be.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If the cost is not paid on demand, the Chairman, Inland Water Transport Authority may, on application by the Conservator and after giving the lessee, licensee or unauthorised occupant, as the case may be, an opportunity of being heard, cause the materials of structures demolished to be sold in auction in such manner as may be prescribed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If the sale proceeds exceed the cost, the excess amount shall be paid to the lessee or the unauthorised occupant.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Recovery of arrears of rent or fee</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. If any rent or fee payable in respect of any land or building has been in arrear on the date of the recovery of possession of such land or building, the amount due on account of such arrears, with interest, if any, accrued thereupon shall be recoverable as public demand under the Public Demands Recovery Act, 1913 (Act III of 1913).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Jurisdiction of Courts barred</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. No Court shall question anything done or purported to have been done by the Conservator under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Indemnity</p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. No suit or other legal proceeding shall lie against the Conservator or any other person in respect of anything which is, in good faith, done or intended to be done under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Delegation of powers</p><p style="text-align: justify;">10. The Conservator, may with, previous approval of the Government, delegate any or all of his powers and functions under this Act to such person as he may think fit and proper.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to make rules</p><p style="text-align: justify;">11. The Government may make rules for carrying out the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
343	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE CONTROL OF ESSENTIAL COMMODITIES (EXTENSION TO THE CHITTAGONG HILL-TRACTS) ORDINANCE, 1970</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE CONTROL OF ESSENTIAL COMMODITIES (EXTENSION TO THE CHITTAGONG HILL-TRACTS) ORDINANCE, 1970 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(EAST PAKISTAN ORDINANCE NO. I OF 1970).[5th January, 1970]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Ordinance to extend the provisions of the 1[ * * *] Control of Essential Commodities Act, 1956, to the district of Chittagong Hill-tracts.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to extend the provisions of the 2[ * * *] Control of Essential Commodities Act, 1956, to the district of Chittagong Hill-tracts;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in pursuance of the Proclamation of the 25th day of March, 1969, read with the Provisional Constitution Order, and in exercise of all powers enabling him in that behalf, the Governor is pleased to make and promulgate the following Ordinance, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the 3[ * * *] Control of Essential Commodities (Extension to the Chittagong Hill-Tracts) Ordinance, 1970.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Application of EP Act I of 1956 to the Chittagong Hill-tracts</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. The 4[ * * *] Control of Essential Commodities Act, 1956, shall apply to the district of Chittagong Hill-tracts.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
344	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE CUSTOMS ACT, 1969 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE CUSTOMS ACT, 1969 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ACT NO. IV OF 1969).[8th  March, 1969]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to consolidate and amend the law relating to customs. 1 2</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to consolidate and amend the law relating to the levy and collection of customs-duties and to provide for other allied matters;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>CHAPTER I</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>PRELIMINARY</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Short title, extent and commencement                1. (1) This Act may be called the Customs Act, 1969.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force on such date as the Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, appoint.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3[ (a) “agent” means any person, including a shipping agent, clearing and forwarding agent, cargo agent, 4[ and freight forwarding agent], licensed under section 207, or any person permitted to transact any business under section 208;]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5[ (aa) “Appellate Tribunal” means the Customs, Excise and ????? ?????? ?? Appellate Tribunal constituted under section 196;]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)
